<dt class="glossary" id="white_horses" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">White horses or whitecaps <span id="Whitecaps"></span></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Foam or spray on wave tops caused by stronger winds (usually above <a href="/wiki/Beaufort_scale" title="Beaufort scale">Force</a> 4).</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="wide_berth" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Wide berth</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To leave room between two ships moored (berthed) to allow space for manoeuver.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="winch" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Winch" title="Winch">Winch</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A small hand operated horizontal geared drum, used to assist in the handling of running gear – wire or rope.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThames_Sailing_Barge_glossary2017_2-166"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThames_Sailing_Barge_glossary2017-2">[2]</a></sup></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="wind-over-tide" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Wind-over-tide</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Sea conditions with a tidal current and a wind in opposite directions, leading to short, heavy seas.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="windage" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Windage" title="Windage">Windage</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Wind resistance of the boat.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="windbound" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Windbound</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A condition wherein the ship is detained in one particular station by contrary winds.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="winding_tackle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Winding tackle</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A tackle formed of two triple blocks or a triple and a double, used to raise heavy loads such as guns and anchors <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArt_of_Rigging184837_51-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArt_of_Rigging184837-51">[50]</a></sup></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="windjammer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Windjammer" title="Windjammer">Windjammer</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A large iron- or steel-hulled square-rigged sailing ship of the late 19th and early 20th centuries with three, four, or five masts, built mainly between the 1870s and 1900 to carry cargo on long voyages.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="windlass" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Windlass" title="Windlass">Windlass</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A winch mechanism, usually with a horizontal axis. Used where mechanical advantage greater than that obtainable by block and tackle was needed (such as raising the anchor on small ships).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArt_of_Rigging184837_51-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArt_of_Rigging184837-51">[50]</a></sup></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="windsail" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Windsail</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A wide tube or funnel of canvas, used to convey a stream of air into the lower compartments of a ship for ventilation.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="windward" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Windward_and_leeward" title="Windward and leeward">Windward</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In the direction that the wind is coming from.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="wing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Wing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">An extension on the side of a vessel. A <i>bridge wing</i> is an open-air extension of the bridge to port or starboard, intended for use in signaling.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="working_up" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Working up</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Training, usually including gunnery practice.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="worm.2C_parcel_and_serve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Worm,_parcel_and_serve" title="Worm, parcel and serve">Worm, parcel and serve</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">To protect a section of rope from chafing by: laying yarns (worming) to fill in the cuntlines, wrapping marline or other small stuff (serving) around it, and stitching a covering of canvas (parceling) over all.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArt_of_Rigging184838_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArt_of_Rigging184838-53">[52]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Y">Y</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_nautical_terms&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Y">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="yacht" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Yacht" title="Yacht">Yacht</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A recreational boat or ship; the term includes <i>sailing yachts</i>, <i>motor yachts</i>, and <i>steam yachts</i>.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="yard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Yard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.  <a href="/wiki/Yard_(sailing)" title="Yard (sailing)">Yard</a>: The horizontal spar from which a square sail is suspended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArt_of_Rigging184838_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArt_of_Rigging184838-53">[52]</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.  A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dockyard" title="Dockyard">dockyard</a> or <a href="/wiki/Shipyard" title="Shipyard">shipyard</a>.</dd>
<dd><span id="Yard_number"></span></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="yard_number" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Yard number</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Each <a href="/wiki/Shipyard" title="Shipyard">shipyard</a> typically numbers the ships that it has built in consecutive order. One use is to identify the ship before a name has been chosen.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="yard_tackle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Yard tackle</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Tackles to raise boats <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArt_of_Rigging184838_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArt_of_Rigging184838-53">[52]</a></sup></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="yardarm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Yard_(sailing)" title="Yard (sailing)">Yardarm</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The very end of a yard. Often mistaken for a "yard", which refers to the entire spar. As in to hang "from the yardarm" and the sun being "over the yardarm" (late enough to have a drink).</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="yarr" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Yarr</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Acknowledgement of an order, or agreement. Also <i>aye, aye</i>.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="yaw" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Ship_motions" title="Ship motions">Yaw</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A vessel's rotational motion about the vertical axis, causing the fore and aft ends to swing from side to side repetitively.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="yawl" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Yawl" title="Yawl">Yawl</a></dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A fore-and-aft rigged sailing vessel with two masts, main and mizzen, the mizzen stepped abaft the rudder post.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="yawl_boat" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Yawl boat</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A rowboat on davits at the stern of the boat.</dd>
</dl>

href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThames_Sailing_Barge_glossary2017_2-47"><sup><i><b>av</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThames_Sailing_Barge_glossary2017_2-48"><sup><i><b>aw</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThames_Sailing_Barge_glossary2017_2-49"><sup><i><b>ax</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThames_Sailing_Barge_glossary2017_2-50"><sup><i><b>ay</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThames_Sailing_Barge_glossary2017_2-51"><sup><i><b>az</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThames_Sailing_Barge_glossary2017_2-52"><sup><i><b>ba</b></i></sup></a> <a
